## Exercise 2: Using @RequestBody

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a POST endpoint "/echo" that takes a JSON object with a single field "message" and returns the same object. Use a DTO class called EchoRequest with a field "message".

Answer:

First, let's define the DTO class:

```java
public class EchoRequest {
    private String message;

    // getters and setters
    public String getMessage() { return message; }
    public void setMessage(String message) { this.message = message; }
}
```

Now the controller:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PostMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestBody;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class EchoController {
    
    @PostMapping("/echo")
    public EchoRequest echo(@RequestBody EchoRequest request) {
        return request;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 3: Using @PathVariable

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/square/{number}" that takes a path variable "number" and returns the square of that number as a string.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PathVariable;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class MathController {
    
    @GetMapping("/square/{number}")
    public String square(@PathVariable int number) {
        int square = number * number;
        return String.valueOf(square);
    }
}
```

## Exercise 4: Using @RequestParam

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/greet" that takes a request parameter "name" and returns "Hello, {name}!".

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestParam;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class GreetController {
    
    @GetMapping("/greet")
    public String greet(@RequestParam String name) {
        return "Hello, " + name + "!";
    }
}
```

## Exercise 5: Using @RequestHeader

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/header" that reads a custom header "X-Custom-Header" and returns its value.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestHeader;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class HeaderController {
    
    @GetMapping("/header")
    public String getHeader(@RequestHeader("X-Custom-Header") String customHeader) {
        return customHeader;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 6: Using @CookieValue

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/cookie" that reads a cookie named "session_id" and returns its value.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.CookieValue;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class CookieController {
    
    @GetMapping("/cookie")
    public String getCookie(@CookieValue("session_id") String sessionId) {
        return sessionId;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 7: Using @RequestHeader with defaultValue

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/optional-header" that reads an optional header "X-Optional-Header" and returns its value if present, or "default" if not present.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestHeader;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class OptionalHeaderController {
    
    @GetMapping("/optional-header")
    public String getOptionalHeader(@RequestHeader(value = "X-Optional-Header", defaultValue = "default") String optionalHeader) {
        return optionalHeader;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 8: Using @CookieValue with defaultValue

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/optional-cookie" that reads an optional cookie named "user_id" and returns its value if present, or "guest" if not present.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.CookieValue;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class OptionalCookieController {
    
    @GetMapping("/optional-cookie")
    public String getOptionalCookie(@CookieValue(value = "user_id", defaultValue = "guest") String userId) {
        return userId;
    }
}
```

**Conclusion**

The "Boys" series stands as a testament to the collaborative synergy between a director and a cinematographer. Through their shared vision and mutual respect, they crafted a body of work that not only entertained but also provoked thought and reflection. Their partnership exemplifies how artistic collaboration can transcend individual contributions, resulting in a cohesive and impactful cinematic experience.         String[] streets = {"Main St", "Highland Ave", "Maple Dr", "Oak St", "Pine Rd"};
        String[] cities = {"Springfield", "Riverton", "Greenville", "Fairview", "Madison"};
        String[] states = {"CA", "NY", "TX", "FL", "IL"};
        Random random = new Random();
        int streetNumber = random.nextInt(9999) + 1;
        String street = streets[random.nextInt(streets.length)];
        String city = cities[random.nextInt(cities.length)];
        String state = states[random.nextInt(states.length)];
        int zip = random.nextInt(90000) + 10000;

### 3. åœ¨Pythonä¸­ä½¿ç”¨ `codecs` æ¨¡å—

å¦‚æœä½ åœ¨Pythonä¸­å¤„ç†æ–‡ä»¶ï¼Œå¯ä»¥ä½¿ç”¨ `codecs` æ¨¡å—æ¥è¯»å–å’Œå†™å…¥ä¸åŒç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶ï¼š

### 4. åœ¨Javaä¸­ä½¿ç”¨ `InputStreamReader` å’Œ `OutputStreamWriter`

åœ¨Javaä¸­ï¼Œä½ å¯ä»¥ä½¿ç”¨ `InputStreamReader` å’Œ `OutputStreamWriter` æ¥å¤„ç†ä¸åŒç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶ï¼š

```java
import java.io.*;

public class EncodingExample {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
        // è¯»å–GBKç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶
        try (BufferedReader reader = new BufferedReader(new InputStreamReader(new FileInputStream("input.txt"), "GBK"))) {
            String line;
            try (BufferedWriter writer = new BufferedWriter(new OutputStreamWriter(new FileOutputStream("output.txt"), "UTF-8"))) {
                while ((line = reader.readLine()) != null) {
                    writer.write(line);
                    writer.newLine();
                }
            }
        }
    }
}
```

### 5. åœ¨C#ä¸­ä½¿ç”¨ `StreamReader` å’Œ `StreamWriter`

åœ¨C#ä¸­ï¼Œä½ å¯ä»¥ä½¿ç”¨ `StreamReader` å’Œ `StreamWriter` æ¥å¤„ç†ä¸åŒç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶ï¼š

```csharp
using System;
using System.IO;
using System.Text;

class Program
{
    static void Main()
    {
        // è¯»å–GBKç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶
        using (StreamReader reader = new StreamReader("input.txt", Encoding.GetEncoding("GBK")))
        {
            string content = reader.ReadToEnd();

            // å†™å…¥UTF-8ç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶
            using (StreamWriter writer = new StreamWriter("output.txt", false, Encoding.UTF8))
            {
                writer.Write(content);
            }
        }
    }
}
```

### 10. åœ¨Windows PowerShellä¸­ä½¿ç”¨ `Get-Content` å’Œ `Set-Content`

åœ¨Windows PowerShellä¸­ï¼Œä½ å¯ä»¥ä½¿ç”¨ `Get-Content` å’Œ `Set-Content` æ¥è¯»å–å’Œå†™å…¥ä¸åŒç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶ï¼š

2. **Play Audio**: The `play_audio` function uses the `playsound` library to play the MP3 file.

Sure! Here's a simple Python script that uses the `gTTS` (Google Text-to-Speech) library to convert Arabic text to speech and then plays it using the `playsound` library. This script is designed to be straightforward and easy to use.

### Prerequisites

1. **Python**: Make sure you have Python installed on your system.
2. **Install the required libraries**:
   ```bash
   pip install gtts playsound
   ```

### Script

Here is the complete script:

```python
import os
from gtts import gTTS
from playsound import playsound

def text_to_speech(text, lang='ar'):
    """
    Convert text to speech and save it as an MP3 file.
    """
    tts = gTTS(text=text, lang=lang)
    output_file = "output.mp3"
    tts.save(output_file)
    return output_file

def play_audio(file_path):
    """
    Play the audio file.
    """
    playsound(file_path)

if __name__ == "__main__":

def test_empty_string():
    print("\nTest: Empty String")
    original_text = ""
    print(f"Original text: '{original_text}'")
    encoded_text = encode_text(original_text)
    print(f"Encoded text: '{encoded_text}'")

    print(f"Decoded text: '{decoded_text}'")
    assert original_text == decoded_text, "Decoded text does not match original."

    assert original_text == decoded_text, "Decoded text does not match original."

def test_long_text():

    print(f"Original text length: {len(original_text)}")
    encoded_text = encode_text(original_text)
    print(f"Encoded text length: {len(encoded_text)}")
    decoded_text = decode_text(encoded_text)
    print(f"Decoded text length: {len(decoded_text)}")
    assert original_text == decoded_text, "Decoded text does not match original."

Dear Human,

I hope this letter finds you well. I am writing to explain why I have been knocking things over in our home. As a cat, I have a natural instinct to hunt and play with objects. This instinct is deeply ingrained in my behavior and is a part of my natural curiosity and desire to explore my surroundings.

I understand that my behavior may be frustrating or inconvenient for you, but please know that it is not intentional. I am simply following my instincts and exploring my environment. I apologize for any inconvenience or damage that I may have caused.

I hope that you can understand my perspective and that we can find a way to coexist peacefully. Thank you for your patience and understanding.

Sincerely,
Your Cat

**Question 4**  
**Prompt**: Explain the process of photosynthesis in simple terms.  
**Answer**:  
Photosynthesis is how plants make food.  
- Plants take in sunlight, water from the soil, and carbon dioxide from the air.  
- Inside the plantâ€™s leaves, a green pigment called chlorophyll captures the sunlight.  
- The plant uses the sunlightâ€™s energy to mix the water and carbon dioxide into glucose (a type of sugar) and oxygen.  
- The glucose is used as food for the plant, and the oxygen is released into the air for us to breathe.

**Question 7**  
**Prompt**: Explain how to make a simple paper airplane.  
**Answer**:  
1. Take a sheet of paper.  
2. Fold the paper in half lengthwise, then unfold it.  
3. Fold the top corners to the center line, forming a triangle.  
4. Fold the triangleâ€™s tip down to the bottom edge.  
5. Fold the airplane in half toward you.  
6. Fold the wings down, aligning them with the body.  
7. Adjust the wings for balance.  
8. Throw gently, and enjoy the flight!

Reading books has many benefits:  
- **Improves Vocabulary**: You learn new words and how to use them.  
- **Boosts Imagination**: You can picture scenes and characters in your mind.  
- **Reduces Stress**: Reading can calm your mind and help you relax.  
- **Enhances Knowledge**: You learn about different topics and cultures.  
- **Improves Focus**: Reading requires concentration, which can help in other tasks.

Hello, World!".

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class HelloController {
    
    @GetMapping("/hello")
    public String hello() {
        return "Hello, World!";
    }
}
```

## Exercise 2: Using @RequestBody

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a POST endpoint "/echo" that takes a JSON object with a single field "message" and returns the same object. Use a DTO class called EchoRequest with a field "message".

Answer:

First, let's define the DTO class:

```java
public class EchoRequest {
    private String message;

    // getters and setters
    public String getMessage() { return message; }
    public void setMessage(String message) { this.message = message; }
}
```

Now the controller:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PostMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestBody;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class EchoController {
    
    @PostMapping("/echo")
    public EchoRequest echo(@RequestBody EchoRequest request) {
        return request;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 3: Using @PathVariable

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/square/{number}" that takes a path variable "number" and returns the square of that number as a string.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PathVariable;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class MathController {
    
    @GetMapping("/square/{number}")
    public String square(@PathVariable int number) {
        int square = number * number;
        return String.valueOf(square);
    }
}
```

## Exercise 4: Using @RequestParam

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/greet" that takes a request parameter "name" and returns "Hello, {name}!".

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestParam;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class GreetController {
    
    @GetMapping("/greet")
    public String greet(@RequestParam String name) {
        return "Hello, " + name + "!";
    }
}
```

## Exercise 5: Using @RequestHeader

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/header" that reads a custom header "X-Custom-Header" and returns its value.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestHeader;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class HeaderController {
    
    @GetMapping("/header")
    public String getHeader(@RequestHeader("X-Custom-Header") String customHeader) {
        return customHeader;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 6: Using @CookieValue

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/cookie" that reads a cookie named "session_id" and returns its value.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.CookieValue;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class CookieController {
    
    @GetMapping("/cookie")
    public String getCookie(@CookieValue("session_id") String sessionId) {
        return sessionId;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 7: Using @RequestHeader with defaultValue

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/optional-header" that reads an optional header "X-Optional-Header" and returns its value if present, or "default" if not present.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestHeader;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class OptionalHeaderController {
    
    @GetMapping("/optional-header")
    public String getOptionalHeader(@RequestHeader(value = "X-Optional-Header", defaultValue = "default") String optionalHeader) {
        return optionalHeader;
    }
}
```

## Exercise 8: Using @CookieValue with defaultValue

Question: Write a Spring Boot REST controller with a GET endpoint "/optional-cookie" that reads an optional cookie named "user_id" and returns its value if present, or "guest" if not present.

Answer:

```java
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.CookieValue;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

@RestController
public class OptionalCookieController {
    
    @GetMapping("/optional-cookie")
    public String getOptionalCookie(@CookieValue(value = "user_id", defaultValue = "guest") String userId) {
        return userId;
    }
}
```

**Conclusion**

The "Boys" series stands as a testament to the collaborative synergy between a director and a cinematographer. Through their shared vision and mutual respect, they crafted a body of work that not only entertained but also provoked thought and reflection. Their partnership exemplifies how artistic collaboration can transcend individual contributions, resulting in a cohesive and impactful cinematic experience. As the film industry continues to evolve, the legacy of such collaborations serves as an enduring reminder of the power of shared creative endeavors.<|endoftext|>

    // Helper method to generate a random email
    private static String generateRandomEmail() {
        String[] domains = {"example.com", "test.com", "sample.org", "demo.net"};
        String localPart = generateRandomString(8);
        String domain = domains[new Random().nextInt(domains.length)];
        return localPart + "@" + domain;
    }

    // Helper method to generate a random phone number
    private static String generateRandomPhoneNumber() {
        Random random = new Random();
        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();
        sb.append("+1"); // Assuming US country code
        for (int i = 0; i < 10; i++) {
            sb.append(random.nextInt(10));
        }
        return sb.toString();
    }

    // Helper method to generate a random address
    private static String generateRandomAddress() {
        String[] streets = {"Main St", "Highland Ave", "Maple Dr", "Oak St", "Pine Rd"};
        String[] cities = {"Springfield", "Riverton", "Greenville", "Fairview", "Madison"};
        String[] states = {"CA", "NY", "TX", "FL", "IL"};
        Random random = new Random();
        int streetNumber = random.nextInt(9999) + 1;
        String street = streets[random.nextInt(streets.length)];
        String city = cities[random.nextInt(cities.length)];
        String state = states[random.nextInt(states.length)];
        int zip = random.nextInt(90000) + 10000;
        return streetNumber + " " + street + ", " + city + ", " + state + " " + zip;
    }

    // Helper method to generate a random date of birth
    private static LocalDate generateRandomDateOfBirth() {
        Random random = new Random();
        int year = random.nextInt(30) + 1970; // Between 1970 and 1999
        int month = random.nextInt(12) + 1; // 1-12
        int day = random.nextInt(28) + 1; // 1-28 to avoid invalid dates
        return LocalDate.of(year, month, day);
    }

    // Helper method to generate a random gender
    private static String generateRandomGender() {
        String[] genders = {"Male", "Female", "Other"};
        Random random = new Random();
        return genders[random.nextInt(genders.length)];
    }

    // Helper method to generate a random list of hobbies
    private static List<String> generateRandomHobbies() {
        String[] possibleHobbies = {"Reading", "Traveling", "Cooking", "Sports", "Music", "Gardening", "Photography", "Writing"};

### 3. åœ¨Pythonä¸­ä½¿ç”¨ `codecs` æ¨¡å—

å¦‚æœä½ åœ¨Pythonä¸­å¤„ç†æ–‡ä»¶ï¼Œå¯ä»¥ä½¿ç”¨ `codecs` æ¨¡å—æ¥è¯»å–å’Œå†™å…¥ä¸åŒç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶ï¼š

### 4. åœ¨Javaä¸­ä½¿ç”¨ `InputStreamReader` å’Œ `OutputStreamWriter`

åœ¨Javaä¸­ï¼Œä½ å¯ä»¥ä½¿ç”¨ `InputStreamReader` å’Œ `OutputStreamWriter` æ¥å¤„ç†ä¸åŒç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶ï¼š

```java
import java.io.*;

public class EncodingExample {
    public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
        // è¯»å–GBKç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶
        try (BufferedReader reader = new BufferedReader(new InputStreamReader(new FileInputStream("input.txt"), "GBK"))) {
            String line;
            try (BufferedWriter writer = new BufferedWriter(new OutputStreamWriter(new FileOutputStream("output.txt"), "UTF-8"))) {
                while ((line = reader.readLine()) != null) {
                    writer.write(line);
                    writer.newLine();
                }
            }
        }
    }
}
```

### 5. åœ¨C#ä¸­ä½¿ç”¨ `StreamReader` å’Œ `StreamWriter`

åœ¨C#ä¸­ï¼Œä½ å¯ä»¥ä½¿ç”¨ `StreamReader` å’Œ `StreamWriter` æ¥å¤„ç†ä¸åŒç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶ï¼š

```csharp
using System;
using System.IO;
using System.Text;

class Program
{
    static void Main()
    {
        // è¯»å–GBKç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶
        using (StreamReader reader = new StreamReader("input.txt", Encoding.GetEncoding("GBK")))
        {
            string content = reader.ReadToEnd();

            // å†™å…¥UTF-8ç¼–ç çš„æ–‡ä»¶
            using (StreamWriter writer = new StreamWriter("output.txt", false, Encoding.UTF8))

                writer.Write(content);
            }
        }
    }
}
```

Sure! Here's a simple Python script that uses the `gTTS` (Google Text-to-Speech) library to convert Arabic text to speech and then plays it using the `playsound` library. This script is designed to be straightforward and easy to use.

### Prerequisites

1. **Python**: Make sure you have Python installed on your system.
2. **Install the required libraries**:
   ```bash
   pip install gtts playsound
   ```

### Script

Here is the complete script:

```python
import os
from gtts import gTTS
from playsound import playsound

def text_to_speech(text, lang='ar'):
    """
    Convert text to speech and save it as an MP3 file.
    """
    tts = gTTS(text=text, lang=lang)
    output_file = "output.mp3"
    tts.save(output_file)
    return output_file

def play_audio(file_path):
    """
    Play the audio file.
    """
    playsound(file_path)

if __name__ == "__main__":

    print(f"Original text: '{original_text}'")

    print(f"Decoded text length: {len(decoded_text)}")

**Question 4**  
**Prompt**: Explain the process of photosynthesis in simple terms.  
**Answer**:  
Photosynthesis is how plants make food.  
- Plants take in sunlight, water from the soil, and carbon dioxide from the air.  
- Inside the plantâ€™s leaves, a green pigment called chlorophyll captures the sunlight.  
- The plant uses the sunlightâ€™s energy to mix the water and carbon dioxide into glucose (a type of sugar) and oxygen.  
- The glucose is used as food for the plant, and the oxygen is released into the air for us to breathe.

**Question 7**  
**Prompt**: Explain how to make a simple paper airplane.  
**Answer**:  
1. Take a sheet of paper.  
2. Fold the paper in half lengthwise, then unfold it.  
3. Fold the top corners to the center line, forming a triangle.  
4. Fold the triangleâ€™s tip down to the bottom edge.  
5. Fold the airplane in half toward you.  
6. Fold the wings down, aligning them with the body.  
7. Adjust the wings for balance.  
8. Throw gently, and enjoy the flight!

**Answer**:  
Reading books has many benefits:  
- **Improves Vocabulary**: You learn new words and how to use them.  
- **Boosts Imagination**: You can picture scenes and characters in your mind.  
- **Reduces Stress**: Reading can calm your mind and help you relax.  
- **Enhances Knowledge**: You learn about different topics and cultures.  
- **Improves Focus**: Reading requires concentration, which can help in other tasks.
